## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the rate of change of concentration (dA_dt) as a function of concentration A and time t, directly corresponding to deriving reaction rate laws in chemical kinetics. Typically, rate laws express dA_dt as a function of A (e.g., zero‑, first‑, second‑order) and may additionally depend explicitly on t if the rate constant varies due to catalyst deactivation or external conditions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero‑order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of A)
- First‑order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A
- Second‑order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2
- General nth‑order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1
- Mixed first and second order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2
- Reversible pseudo‑first‑order: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A
- Half‑order kinetics (e.g., radical recombination): dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5
- Substrate inhibition (Langmuir–Hinshelwood with inhibition): dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + c2 * A + c3 * A**2)
- Time‑dependent exponential decay of rate constant: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * exp(c2 * t)
- Time‑dependent power‑law rate constant: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (t + c2)**c3
- Zero‑order with time decay: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t)
- Linear time dependence (external addition/removal): dA_dt = c0 + c1 * t
- Autocatalytic logistic‑type: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (can produce sigmoidal concentration profiles)
- Exponential concentration dependence (thermal runaway): dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * A)
- Square‑root with offset: dA_dt = c0 * (A + c1)**0.5

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Rate independent of A (constant dA_dt) → zero‑order kinetics, often due to catalyst saturation or light‑limited reaction.
- Proportionality to A^n → nth‑order reaction; n=0.5 (half‑order) indicates radical recombination or dissociation‑limited steps.
- Linear form dA_dt = c0 + c1*A → reversible reaction where the reverse rate is pseudo‑constant, or parallel zero‑ and first‑order steps.
- Rational law with denominator polynomial (A + c1 + c2*A²) → heterogeneous catalytic mechanism with substrate inhibition (Langmuir–Hinshelwood).
- Multiplicative exponential or power‑law factor in t → time‑varying rate constant from catalyst deactivation, temperature drift, or light‑source decay.
- Concave‑down polynomial dA_dt = c0*A*(c1 - A) → autocatalysis or logistic growth, producing a maximum rate at intermediate A.
- Explicit t without A → external sink/source term, representing controlled addition or removal independent of current concentration.
- Combined polynomial and exponential terms in t and A → coupled time‑ and concentration‑dependent mechanisms, e.g., accelerating rate with decay.
- Square‑root or rational exponent on A → kinetic orders from complex mechanisms with chain reactions or equilibrium pre‑steps.

GT: -c0*A*exp(-c1*_s*t) + c2*_w*cos(log(A + c3))
Candidates evaluated: 63

The Ground Truth (GT) is mathematically:
\[
GT = \alpha \cdot A \cdot e^{\beta \cdot t} + \gamma \cdot \cos\!\big(\ln(A + 1)\big)
\]
with fixed constants \(\alpha = -0.73177...,\; \beta = -0.08162...,\; \gamma = 0.84034...\)).  
The two essential basis functions are:
1. \(A \cdot e^{\text{(constant)} \cdot t}\)
2. \(\cos\!\big(\ln(A + \text{constant})\big)\)  (or a phase‑shifted sine equivalent).

Now we examine all 63 candidates under the rules:
- We may assign **any real numbers** to candidate constants, **including zero**.
- Extra additive terms can be eliminated by setting their multiplicative constants to zero.
- \(\sin(x + \pi/2) = \cos(x)\) allows a sine term with appropriate phase to become cosine.
- The inside of the logarithm can be scaled: \(\ln(A \cdot c + 1)\) becomes \(\ln(A+1)\) by setting \(c=1\).

**Candidates 1–60** all share the following structure (after possible constant assignments):
- A term of the form \(A \cdot (\text{const}) \cdot e^{\text{const} \cdot t}\) (or a trivial variant like \(A^{c_0} \cdot c_1 \cdot e^{c_2 t}\) with \(c_0=1\)).
- A term of the form \(\text{const} \cdot \sin\!\big(c_a \ln(A \cdot c_b + 1) + c_\phi\big)\) or \(\text{const} \cdot \cos\!\big(c_a \ln(A \cdot c_b + 1)\big)\).
- Other additive terms that are multiplied by a free constant (e.g., \(c \cdot \log(\dots),\; c \cdot t,\; c \cdot e^{A},\; c \cdot \sqrt{A}\), rational functions, etc.).

By setting the “extra” constants to zero (e.g., \(c=0\)), all unwanted terms disappear.  
By setting \(c_a = 1,\; c_b = 1\), the logarithmic argument becomes \(\ln(A+1)\).  
If the trigonometric function is sine, setting the phase \(c_\phi = \pi/2\) turns it into cosine.  
The coefficients of the remaining two terms are free to match the GT’s numerical values (including negative signs).

Thus **each of the first 60 candidates can be reduced exactly to the GT** by appropriate constant assignments.

**Candidates 61–63** lack any trigonometric function of a logarithm. They contain only logarithmic terms like \(\log(A \cdot \text{const} + 1)\). Because \(\cos\!\big(\ln(A+1)\big)\) is linearly independent from polynomials and logarithms, no combination of constants can turn a pure logarithm into the required cosine term. Therefore these three candidates **cannot** match the GT.

Since at least one candidate (indeed many) exactly matches the Ground Truth after constant assignment, the final verdict is:

[MATCH FOUND]

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.731770189531933*A*exp(-0.0816213403667534*t) + 0.840340504979681*cos(log(A + 1))`

This has two terms:
1. `A*exp(c*t)` term (exponential decay in t, linear in A)
2. `cos(log(A + 1))` term (no t dependence)

No constant offset term (though one could argue c2=0 is allowed if a candidate has an additive constant).

Let me analyze each candidate's structural form to see if it can reduce to the GT by choosing constants.

**Key structural requirements:**
- Term 1: `A*exp(k*t)` ✓
- Term 2: `cos(log(A+1))` — note that `sin(x + π/2) = cos(x)`, so `sin(c*log(A*c+1) + c)` can match `cos(log(A+1))`
- No other terms that can't be zeroed out
